    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/394811-this-book-was-amazing-true-to-life-and">This book was amazing, true to life, and Vera is a dynamic, edgy, and unstoppable character. One thing though -- what was in the envelope??? Did I miss something???? She opens the cigar box, reads the napkins, goes to the police, but nobody apparently opens the envelope?? Did the author forget that detail, or was it deliberate?</a>
</div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer204658661" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11738508524904892165">I have been lucky enough to read a LOT of great books this year and up until now I had a clear I-shine-above-the-rest favourite: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road' title='On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>On the Jellicoe Road</a>. Though I am actually going to be daring enough to say to all you Marchetta-obsessed bookaholics that for me <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz' title='Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> could compete with the sad and beautiful emotional turmoil I felt for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road' title='On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta' rel='nofollow noopener'>On the Jellicoe Road</a>.<br/><br/>There are two young adult topics that always make me think "oh, not again", and they are:<br/><br/>1) teen pregnancy, and<br/>2) coping with</span>
  <span id="freeText11738508524904892165" style="display:none">I have been lucky enough to read a LOT of great books this year and up until now I had a clear I-shine-above-the-rest favourite: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Jellicoe Road</a>. Though I am actually going to be daring enough to say to all you Marchetta-obsessed bookaholics that for me <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> could compete with the sad and beautiful emotional turmoil I felt for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Jellicoe Road</a>.<br /><br />There are two young adult topics that always make me think "oh, not again", and they are:<br /><br />1) teen pregnancy, and<br />2) coping with the death of a loved one<br /><br />These subjects are so overdone that the mere thought of tackling yet another piece of this melodramatic drivel makes my head ache... but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> is probably the best book I have ever read that involves death and the aftermath of it; all the sorrow and guilt and "what ifs" told in such a beautiful way. In fact, I honestly cannot think of a novel that handles it better.<br /><br />Anyone can put pretty words in the right order, but it takes a really talented author to make you truly <i>feel</i>. They are the kind of writers who know how to make you love, hate or just want to have sex with a character. Here, I felt everything that Vera felt; it was very emotionally draining but ultimately more rewarding at the end - I love those books that truly affect me, they stay with me far longer than the rest.<br /><br />Charlie, as well as Vera, was a remarkable character. He reminded me of a debate I had recently about <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6185.Wuthering_Heights" title="Wuthering Heights by Emily Brontë" rel="nofollow noopener">Wuthering Heights</a> and, in particular, Heathcliff. I've always said that the best actors are those who can make you feel sorry for an evil and twisted character, that can make you understand even if redemption is impossible... I feel it's the same with authors. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4191.Emily_Bront_" title="Emily Brontë" rel="nofollow noopener">Emily Brontë</a> created a character who was a violent monster, yet the way she explores the unloved childhood he endured always makes me feel nothing but sympathy for a man who is cruel because he's been shown nothing else. <br /><br />I love complex characters. There are few, if any, people in this world who can be called something so simple as "good" or "bad".<br /><br />This is why I loved Charlie and all his stupid fuckedupness. Charlie makes so many mistakes and he frequently gets it all wrong. In the hands of a weaker author, you could easily hate him... but you don't. Yes, this is a novel about death and yes, this is a novel about friendship and love and the fine line between right and wrong... but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> is first and foremost an exploration of two complex individuals who are two of the most well-drawn characters I have come across in the young adult genre. Huge thanks to Tatiana, without whom I would never have read this book.<br /><br /><a href="http://emilymay.me" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11738508524904892165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_69382760" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/69382760" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/69382760?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=printz">printz</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer69382760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11501179259701940276">As seen on <a href='http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/please-ignore-vera-dietz-by-as-king1.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Readventurer</a><br/><br/><b>So, this novel just got awarded <i>Printz Honor</i>. I guess I wasn't hyping it for nothing. Please, fellow goodreaders, check this book out!</b><br/><br/>Let me just get this out of the way, I am glad I gave <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1651879.A_S__King' title='A.S. King' rel='nofollow noopener'>A.S. King</a> another chance. I liked her debut novel (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3873328.The_Dust_of_100_Dogs' title='The Dust of 100 Dogs by A.S. King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Dust of 100 Dogs</a>) OK, for its creativity and originality, but I wasn't wowed by it. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz' title='Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> is a better, even though more mainstream, YA novel. <br/><br/>I don't know how it happened, but I've read quite a few YA books abou</span>
  <span id="freeText11501179259701940276" style="display:none">As seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/please-ignore-vera-dietz-by-as-king1.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a><br /><br /><b>So, this novel just got awarded <i>Printz Honor</i>. I guess I wasn't hyping it for nothing. Please, fellow goodreaders, check this book out!</b><br /><br />Let me just get this out of the way, I am glad I gave <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1651879.A_S__King" title="A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">A.S. King</a> another chance. I liked her debut novel (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3873328.The_Dust_of_100_Dogs" title="The Dust of 100 Dogs by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dust of 100 Dogs</a>) OK, for its creativity and originality, but I wasn't wowed by it. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> is a better, even though more mainstream, YA novel. <br /><br />I don't know how it happened, but I've read quite a few YA books about death and grief over the last couple of months (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1832749.I_Heart_You__You_Haunt_Me" title="I Heart You, You Haunt Me by Lisa Schroeder" rel="nofollow noopener">I Heart You, You Haunt Me</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7558747.Revolution" title="Revolution by Jennifer Donnelly" rel="nofollow noopener">Revolution</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8221077.Amy___Roger_s_Epic_Detour" title="Amy &amp; Roger's Epic Detour by Morgan Matson" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy &amp; Roger's Epic Detour</a>), however <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> is definitely the one I enjoyed the most. <br /><br />Vera's long-time childhood friend Charlie is dead. She is hurt by his death, but her feelings are ambiguous. Their relationship has been difficult and not always happy, maybe they even hated each other at some point. They used to be so close and yet so separated by their preconceived notions that a romance between them would never work. After all, they both have so much emotional baggage. Vera has to work through many deliciously convoluted aspects of her friendship with Charlie in her mind to finally find peace with him...<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> is the kind of story I love to read the most in YA fiction. It is not over-burdened with romance, where a boy miraculously solves all heroine's problems, it is character driven. Vera is a multi-dimensional character, she has to face her past and deal with her mistakes and regrets in regard to Charlie. Her grief is palpable, but not expressed in hysterical fits and throwing herself around in despair, like it often is in teen lit. Vera's actions speak for it. Her inner world is complex - there are issues she has to deal with that add another layer to this already great story - how can she live up to her father's expectations? how can she get over her mother's abandonment? how can she overcome her seemingly pre-written destiny?<br /><br />The more I think about this novel, the more I like it. It is not as quirky as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3873328.The_Dust_of_100_Dogs" title="The Dust of 100 Dogs by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Dust of 100 Dogs</a>, there are no pirates, magic dust or doggy lessons, but it is unique in its own way. I like that Zen Buddhism wisdom is added into the story. There is a ghost who sheds some light on the events. And there is the Pagoda with some opinions of her own. It all works beautifully together. As a whole, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> is just one clever novel. <br /><br />P.S. Who knew pizza delivery business was such a dangerous occupation? I will absolutely never, under any circumstances, do it, knowing now that there are people who open their doors to delivery people with no pants on and in "full alert."</span>
  <a data-text-id="11501179259701940276" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1313939602" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1313939602" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1313939602?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘ by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/19112398-sarah">Sarah</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fave-ya-and-fantasy">fave-ya-and-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=my-kindle-challenges-me">my-kindle-challenges-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1313939602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4852780150719662646"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452556254i/17708101._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>When he was a child in his foster home, my father wasn't allowed to eat butter</b>. Every day he would see the family children eat it at breakfast, but never once did he break the rule. People in nowhere town, nowhere country France never stopped reminding him that he didn't belong : part Algerian, part Parisian (like a different nationality for them really), he was the kid parents warned their children against, because god forbid any kind of open-mindedness. In the sixties, difference was not a goo</span>
  <span id="freeText4852780150719662646" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452556254i/17708101._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>When he was a child in his foster home, my father wasn't allowed to eat butter</b>. Every day he would see the family children eat it at breakfast, but never once did he break the rule. People in nowhere town, nowhere country France never stopped reminding him that he didn't belong : part Algerian, part Parisian (like a different nationality for them really), he was the kid parents warned their children against, because god forbid any kind of open-mindedness. In the sixties, difference was not a good way to go. When my mother told me this, I cried. I cried because I had no idea. I knew that my father's childhood wasn't all sunshines and rainbows but he never liked to talk about it, and I didn't press him. Truth is, I always thought that I'd had the time to sit down and really talk someday. <i>Later</i>. <br><br>I was wrong, because now it's too late, and that feeling? All frustration and guilt and anger and love. <b>Reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> felt like that, and this story reached to old and hidden parts of me I didn't even remembered.</b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452555750i/17708074._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is my second book from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1651879.A_S__King" title="A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">A.S. King</a>, and by far the strongest. First she managed to <b>perfectly capture the essence of grief</b> : indeed it's rarely devoid of anger - blind, unfair anger we almost never see pictured in books - and that explains partly why I could connect so strongly. People don't warn you how mad you are when someone you love die. Sadness you expect, but anger? No, and it's a shame really, because you can't think clear and guilt is never far. You think you shouldn't be angry. You think there's a problem with you, somehow. Don't. <br><br><b>This is realistic fiction at its finest, that is to say, raw and painful and crazy and beautiful</b>. See, I'm not stranger to grief, and yet, (or because of it) books that deal with grief often piss me off so much that I've been delaying reading Vera's story for more than a year now. I should have trusted my friends, because this story is nothing like the others I read before. What I have a hard time to stand in that kind of books is the "purposeful way" the death of a loved one is often used. <b>It's as if they would make us believe that we only lose people we love to find our destiny or some shit. Fuck that. Sorry guys, I'm a down-to-earth bitch</b> (sorry mum, I tried!). <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1651879.A_S__King" title="A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">A.S. King</a> adds so many anecdotes that made me pause and think, "oh, yes, <i>that</i>". The way you can't help but imagine how it goes, under the earth, even if you know you shouldn't. The way you find yourself speaking alone or consider completely impossible things. Your mind is reeling, but truth is, sometimes there's no answers. Sometimes you have to go on to find them, and here lies the beauty of Vera's story.<br><br>The story is organized with chapters alternating between Vera's life in present time - after Charlie, her best friend, died - and flashbacks where we come to see how their relationship evolved during their childhood and their adolescence. <b>All the events intricate perfectly and I found the way the story was written really wonderful because everything made sense</b>. We think we know where the story is going, but as in real life, the journey is more important than anything here. And little by little, we realize that we didn't really know what to expect in fact - This story surprised me. <br><br>If you're not new to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1651879.A_S__King" title="A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">A.S. King</a>, you know that she is more likely to insert a paranormal side in her stories. If the dreams bothered me a little in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9711714.Everybody_Sees_the_Ants" title="Everybody Sees the Ants by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Everybody Sees the Ants</a>, I have to say that it worked perfectly here. But then, this is Charlie, and I may be partial. I don't care.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452555750i/17708075._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Both main characters are unlikeable and yet so endearing. I loved them fiercely</b>. First of all, Charlie. Aw, Charlie, what a fucked-up you were. What a bunch of self-loathing, devil may care charm, unforgettable male-lead you are. I'm warning you here : you won't agree with everything he did or said, but you won't be able to stop yourself from loving him. I couldn't. You won't be able to stop yourself from hating him, either. He's messed-up, an asshole, and his actions made me want to slap him - really - sometimes. But the important is, his flaws aren't romanticized. We're never served some crappy romance crap where unforgivable behavior is condoned. It isn't. <br><br>As for <b>Vera</b>, the better way to express my feelings is to say that I could understand her : she is flawed, broken, but strong and willing to do anything she can to go on and to refuse hypocrisy. Yet she <i>is</i> judgmental. She <i>is</i> delusional. I won't deny any of that, but she's <i>more</i>. As I already said countless times, I don't care about flaws if the characters are multi-layered. In the end, I really, really liked her because she was real and incredibly brave yet sometimes so scared. This is reality, people. <b>We aren't adjectives but complex human beings</b>. She made mistakes, didn't act when she had to to protect the ones she loves, but she is aware of that. Every fucking second of her life.<br><br>These characters never failed to make me feel deeply, and <b>I am amazed of the depth and complexity of the relationships pictured</b>. Vera and Charlie, Vera and her dad, Charlie and his parents - nothing's useless, everything's three dimensional and kinda messed-up. I loved it. <br><br>How can we escape our "destiny"? Can we, really? What of self-fulfilling prophecies? See, when I was in College I worked a lot about that kind of things - because our self-confidence is also linked to our teachers' remarks, for better or for worse - and this is something I really care about. That's why I found really interesting that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1651879.A_S__King" title="A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">A.S. King</a> chose to deal with it, and in my opinion she did a great job showing that everything is always more complicated than we think : what part of our unconscious fights against the path we don't want to follow? What part of the collective unconscious convinces us that we are going to repeat our parents', our background's mistakes whatever efforts we make? <br><br>How far goes the influence of others? Should we <i>ignore</i> them? <br><br>So many characters in this book struggle against what they think are their destiny : Vera, her father, Charlie. I couldn't help but care for them, so, so much. My only complaint would be that I would have loved for the story to contain other strong female characters. I missed them. <br><br><b>Alright now, forget everything I wrote. Just FORGET IT. The truth, the real truth? I cried like a fucking baby.</b> More and more along the way, and it wasn't because some smart-ass decided that cancer kids were hot or some shit. It wasn't even because Charlie dies, because really, THAT'S IN THE BLURB, ANNA. No. I cried out of rage, out of stupid decisions and SO MUCH WASTE. I cried because I can't even count how many people Charlie reminded me. I cried because FOR FUCK SAKE, CHARLIE. I cried for Vera's dad. I cried for all these kids who have no idea what they can do with their lives - and I don't fucking care how lame that sounds. <br><br>I laughed, too. A lot. I'm sure it counts somewhere? <br><br>To sum-up, <b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> is an astounding book</b> that kept me captive - for real, I had to stop yesterday because it was 3am and ANNA YOU HAVE SCHOOL TOMORROW! I thought about it all day long and jumped on the very first occasion to resume it. Now, rare are the books that have such a great power on me. I wasn't completely satisfied in the end, but who cares? I wanted more, but who cares? Some revelations let me down, but who cares?<br><br>... <b>I'm still immensely impressed.</b> *bows*<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="4852780150719662646" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_229319259" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229319259" />
    <a title="Reynje" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje"><img alt="Reynje" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473722441p2/5590906.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229319259?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reynje" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reynje" href="/user/show/5590906-reynje">Reynje</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8732024-please-ignore-vera-dietz">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229319259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16142224182526655075"><blockquote>
  <b>There was a reason Charlie was such a bright blazing sun. He came from endless cold, black space.</b>
</blockquote>I couldn’t sleep after finishing <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz' title='Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a>.<br/><br/>I gave up on trying to untangle my emotional reaction from my critical thoughts, all hopelessly snarled together with lingering question marks, and just lay staring into the dark. The story refused to seep quietly into my consciousness, to be filed away neatly into a mental catalogue: <i>good writing, interesting characters, believable dialog</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16142224182526655075" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>There was a reason Charlie was such a bright blazing sun. He came from endless cold, black space.</b>
</blockquote>I couldn’t sleep after finishing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a>.<br /><br />I gave up on trying to untangle my emotional reaction from my critical thoughts, all hopelessly snarled together with lingering question marks, and just lay staring into the dark. The story refused to seep quietly into my consciousness, to be filed away neatly into a mental catalogue: <i>good writing, interesting characters, believable dialogue</i> etc, etc. <br /><br />Instead, it kept twisting around in my mind, scenes replaying and looping. Possible interpretations were bound up messily in my own personal experiences and beliefs. Vera, Charlie, Ken, Jenny – they were characters, but I realised that over the course of the book they had become real to me. And their stories wouldn’t let me sleep. <br /><br />How much of who we are is unconsciously pre-determined? I don’t mean this in a “destiny” or “fate” sense. Rather, how much of us is shaped by genetics, deeply hardwired into our blood and bones and minds? How much by the environment we live in everyday, the people who surround us? And how much by our beliefs – the things we hold to be so fundamentally true about ourselves that they become in effect self-fulfilling prophecies? Do we write our own futures by making the choice to accept certain assumptions or opinions of others, without questioning whether in fact they are true? <br /><br />I couldn’t stop wondering about Vera and Charlie’s friendship – and why it played out the way it did. As the story unfolds through a series of viewpoints, flashbacks, flowcharts and interludes from a talking pagoda, there is a growing sense of inevitability. Each part of the story, each event, each nail Charlie’s coffin, to be blunt, almost seems to be set in inexorable motion by the events immediately preceding, by the choices the characters make. And yet how much of this might have been different – if someone spoke up, if someone changed their mind, if someone decided not to believe the thing they’d been told all their lives? Would Vera and Charlie’s lives and relationship have taken a different path? Or was this outcome always bound to happen, by virtue of persistent human nature? <br /><br />At the end, I was overwhelmed with sadness for all of them. And yet I still felt a sincere appreciation for this story, a love for it because it was so honest and real. Because few books manage to convey how very possible it is to love someone and hate them all at the same time, for the people closest to us to inflict the worst kind of pain. <br /><br />Prose-wise, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> is effortless to read. Thematically, it’s not. The voices, particularly Vera’s, are exceptionally genuine and I found myself connecting to her much more than I expected I would. While she is a mostly undemonstrative character, choosing to lay low and will attention away from her, the raw pain and conflict is palpable in her words. The sadness bleeds through, leaching from a well of betrayal, abandonment, misunderstanding and hurt. <blockquote>
  <b>”And so, for all six years she’s been gone, I have $337 to show for having a mother. Dad says that thirty-seven bucks is good interest. He doesn’t see the irony in that.”</b>
</blockquote> Needless to say, I really loved the writing in this book – it was poignant without pretention, emotive without being heavy.<blockquote>
  <b>“Because with Charlie, nothing was ever easy. Everything was windswept and octagonal and finger-combed. Everything was difficult and odd, and the theme songs all had minor chords.”</b>
</blockquote> For a story that tackles death, abuse and alcoholism amongst other things, for the most part King takes a remarkably even-handed approach that feels open and not gratuitous. (There are some other messages <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[around pet ownership <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> in the novel where I felt perhaps King may have been speaking more to her personal opinion – and they came across rather more awkwardly.) I’m loathe to apply the term gritty here, because to be honest I think what King is showing us is simply reality (in terms of the issues it addresses, not the anthropomorphic landmarks, stripper dream sequences and pickles), and the reality is that life isn’t polished and smooth. That tragedy happens all the time. Often, right next door. <br /><br />From reading other reviews of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> I had foreknowledge of some of the more unusual aspects of the story (narrators who shouldn’t physically be able to speak etc) so I didn’t find these elements distracting. If anything, I think I had mentally prepared myself for much more “quirk”, so I was pleasantly surprised by how much I felt myself connecting to the story. I even came to view the speeches from the pagoda as something of a comforting, solid presence in the story amid the increasingly unsettled events and emotions surrounding it. <br /><br />Where I found <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> wanting was in its resolution. I was happy with where the story left most of the characters, but I felt it was a little unrealistic in its timing – what had been a festering wound seemed to heal a little too quickly to be totally believable. I definitely think that the characters would have reached this point eventually – but not with the apparent ease and swiftness with which the book seems to present the situation. <br /><br />Finally, I have to agree with one of my readalong<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229313506" rel="nofollow noopener"> partners-in-crime</a> and say that there is a quite the aura of a cult classic around this book. The execution is slightly unusual, but the story strikes at the heart of intensely relatable and moving subject matter. This may sound contradictory, but this book broke my heart and I loved it. <br /><br />Thanks to my lovely readalong ladies, Shirley Marr, Lisa O and Maja!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16142224182526655075" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_206994192" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206994192" />
    <a title="Limonessa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa"><img alt="Limonessa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1424025988p2/4147373.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206994192?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Limonessa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Limonessa" href="/user/show/4147373-limonessa">Limonessa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375896170" href="/book/show/9476470-please-ignore-vera-dietz">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Limonessa by: </span>
      readalong with the amazing Shirley, Reynje and Maja 
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4147373-limonessa?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer206994192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15557382822970464052">Talk about a heartbreak. I'll have to read at least TEN predictable, fluffy, instalovish, lovetrianglish light-hearted books to recover from this one. <br/><br/>The main voice is Vera's, an 18 y.o student/pizza deliverer who lives alone with her father and whose best friend Charlie has just died. We don't really know how or why, nor do we know why Vera seems to be so royally pissed at him:<br/><br/><i>"Let me tell you - if you think your best friend dying is a bitch, try your best friend dying after he screws you over</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15557382822970464052" style="display:none">Talk about a heartbreak. I'll have to read at least TEN predictable, fluffy, instalovish, lovetrianglish light-hearted books to recover from this one. <br /><br />The main voice is Vera's, an 18 y.o student/pizza deliverer who lives alone with her father and whose best friend Charlie has just died. We don't really know how or why, nor do we know why Vera seems to be so royally pissed at him:<br /><br /><i>"Let me tell you - if you think your best friend dying is a bitch, try your best friend dying after he screws you over. It's a bitch like no other."</i><br /><br />If you've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3097601.Suicide_Notes" title="Suicide Notes by Michael Thomas Ford" rel="nofollow noopener">Suicide Notes</a> (and if you haven't, shame on you) then you'll recognize the narrative strategy in the "revealing" flashbacks. We are introduced to the story when the main events have already taken place, in this case Charlie's death, and we are completely left in the dark about the motives.Through a reconstruction of often terrible memories and revelations we gradually discover the circumstances and the truth. <br /><br />This is not a book that aims at making you feel better about yourself or society or that will leave you with a happy feeling in your heart. This is a testament to bad parenting, bad choices, bad environment, bad genes and the struggle of a girl to try to prove them all wrong. It's a book where the main characters, Charlie, Vera, Ken are portrayed in all shades of grey, where there is no absolute good or bad (well, except for Jenny and Ken's mother who are the essence of evil). At some point or another, I got angry with all of them in turns and then tearfully forgave them all. I felt for Ken, Vera's Dad, a man whose best was never enough and who was never taught to love. I felt for Vera, because it is not easy to grow up in a situation where you are the product of your messed up parents and have to bear their cross on your back your whole life. But most of all, I felt for Charlie, because he's the one who couldn't escape his very messed up situation. He didn't make it, I felt like he <i>couldn't</i> make it and he made all the wrong choices, victim of his low self-esteem, self-loathing and poor judgement. <br />And as far as choices go, I keep on thinking: would none of that have happened - or maybe not tragically so - if Vera had chosen to tell the truth from the beginning? Or would it have been different had Vera's parents not turned their head the other way and taught Vera to <i>ignore</i>, no matter what? This book certainly raises some ethical questions which are, at the same time, both obvious AND controversial. Honesty and altruism should be social givens but they seem to go against the trend, at least in this society. <br /><br />The book is not a 5 star for me for mainly two reasons: <br /><br />- I didn't like how the Vera/Dad relationship got dealt with in the end. You don't solve deeply rooted family problems by going to see a shrink FOUR times and by role-playing once. You just don't. The ending felt so out of place in respect to the general tone of the book that it felt like I was suddenly reading another book.<br /><br />- I didn't like the gratuitous propaganda against having a pet. Especially from the pagoda's side. I don't need to be reminded that the food I buy for my puppy could feed a starving child. I mean, it could be true, but this is not the place. On the same note, I didn't like the presence of a skinhead guy to represent the bad, crazy guy. It just felt superfluous and judgmental. Those were two instances where the author tried to feed us a piece of her mind which I didn't want.<br /><br />Nevertheless <i>Please ignore Vera Dietz</i> is a fantastic book I recommend to everybody. It's raw, shocking and so heart-breaking that it makes you look at your kids with different eyes, in my opinion. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15557382822970464052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review206994192">

<div id="review_2060264487" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2060264487" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2060264487?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=death">death</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2060264487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11738937233638027911">Please Ignore Vera Dietz is the book that kick-started A.S. King’s career as a writer. I can see why it won a Printz award. Having read seven books from this author, I can safely say that she’s a YA writer you’ll want to check out if you need dept in your reads and like a little obscurity. <br/><br/>What makes this author stand out from the dozens of thousands other YA authors is her creative and touching inclusion of magical realism at unexpected places. I say touching because those magical realism eleme</span>
  <span id="freeText11738937233638027911" style="display:none">Please Ignore Vera Dietz is the book that kick-started A.S. King’s career as a writer. I can see why it won a Printz award. Having read seven books from this author, I can safely say that she’s a YA writer you’ll want to check out if you need dept in your reads and like a little obscurity. <br /><br />What makes this author stand out from the dozens of thousands other YA authors is her creative and touching inclusion of magical realism at unexpected places. I say touching because those magical realism elements are usually powerful in terms of emotions and serve a strong purpose to the plot by affecting the characters, thus pushing them to ponder their problems and ultimately come to terms with different issues. <br /><br />Having said that and though I acknowledge A.S. King’s beautiful lyrical writing, she isn’t one to go straight to the point. She likes to go round and round exploring layers of surfaces before going back to the beginning to reveal the truth. It’s good to be three-dimensional for sure…. But basically, she can be repetitive. Unfortunately, this is why I couldn’t like this more. I normally read her books in one day, but with this one—and believe me I’ve wanted to read it for months—I had no problem putting it down for another book. <br /><br />This book deals, among other things, with the death of a former best friend. Charlie and Vera have known each other since they were toddlers, but adolescence has affected the both of them in similar and yet such different ways that they’ve lost each other. And then Charlie dies and Vera doesn’t know how to feel. Should she tell the truth about his death or take revenge on him? I felt very connected to Vera but less to Charlie, as his chapters are scarce and he is more of the love-to-hate type than the love-to-love one. However, it isn’t so simple. There is much to him that isn’t as it seems. <br /><br />I don’t think you should ignore this book, even if it begs you to. Hehe. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>

<div id="review_130380553" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/130380553" />
    <a title="Flannery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/652877-flannery"><img alt="Flannery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312843258p2/652877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/130380553?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flannery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flannery" href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Flannery by: </span>
      Tatiana, Catie, Jo
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=young-adult-teen">young-adult-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=kcls">kcls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=wishlist-for-dtbs-to-keep">wishlist-for-dtbs-to-keep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=reviewed-2011">reviewed-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer130380553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12017065802757903856">Vera Dietz is a good person. This book is like watching Vera in the gallows being pelted with tomatoes until she is finally released to go on her way. Her lifelong best friend Charlie just passed away under somewhat mysterious circumstances, the town blames him for something which tarnishes his reputation, and Vera is being harassed by some of her schoolmates. The thing about Vera, and I absolutely loved her as a character, is that she just deals with it. She is angry with Charlie, she hates him</span>
  <span id="freeText12017065802757903856" style="display:none">Vera Dietz is a good person. This book is like watching Vera in the gallows being pelted with tomatoes until she is finally released to go on her way. Her lifelong best friend Charlie just passed away under somewhat mysterious circumstances, the town blames him for something which tarnishes his reputation, and Vera is being harassed by some of her schoolmates. The thing about Vera, and I absolutely loved her as a character, is that she just deals with it. She is angry with Charlie, she hates him and she loves him and she realizes it is possible to feel both of those feelings at the same time. She resents all the choices that he made that led up to his death and she resents herself for not doing something more to help him. <br /><br />Vera’s father has been raising her as a single dad since his wife skipped town. The narration, which skips between Vera, her father, Charlie, and even a town architectural landmark, lets us know that the main characters are all worried about being foregone conclusions. Are we all destined to be like our parents or what everyone tells us we’ll become? I truly hope not, not because my parents aren’t lovely people but because that would be a sad state of affairs. Vera’s father Ken struggles with Vera drinking because he is an alcoholic. Vera worries about becoming like her absent mother. Charlie worried about becoming an abuser like his father. We all worry about something. <br /><br />I can absolutely see why this book was a Printz Honor pick. Vera’s voice is very matter-of-fact but her contemplations and commentary were funny at times, poignant at others, and she keeps a level-head for almost the entire book. She deals with her missteps while still trying to figure out how to grieve for her best friend who was mostly lost to her even before he died. I’m reading another book right now where someone has just passed away (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7979073.Minding_Frankie" title="Minding Frankie by Maeve Binchy" rel="nofollow noopener">Minding Frankie</a>) and a character talks about that saying that a person remembered through memories or mentions is never truly gone. Or how Jacob Coote tells Josie Alibrandi that he dealt with his mother’s death by crying at the memories until one day, he could smile or laugh at them. (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/82436.Looking_for_Alibrandi" title="Looking for Alibrandi by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Looking for Alibrandi</a>) This book takes place before Vera has come to terms with the loss but by the end, it was clear that she was no longer using a band-aid to cover up a gaping wound. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6665671.Please_Ignore_Vera_Dietz" title="Please Ignore Vera Dietz by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Please Ignore Vera Dietz</a> was very successful in audio format. The narrator’s Vera was perfect and I appreciated the fact that male narrators pitched in for the points in the story not narrated by Vera. I’m curious whether the descriptions of flow charts in the narration were actually flow chart images in the book so maybe someone who knows can chime in with an answer. I would absolutely recommend it in this format.<br /><br />I’m excited to check out A.S. King’s upcoming <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9711714.Everybody_Sees_the_Ants" title="Everybody Sees the Ants by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Everybody Sees The Ants</a>. After reading a review that said it had similar themes, I’m hoping that it will be sufficiently different but retain a similar tone. This one was sad but weirdly hopeful. It was about 4.5/5 for me. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12017065802757903856" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5090698884079999925"><b>I am a little confused! But also a little bit pleased with this one!</b> I confess I've read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23203744.I_Crawl_Through_It' title='I Crawl Through It by A.S. King' rel='nofollow noopener'>I Crawl Through It</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28588459.Still_Life_with_Tornado' title='Still Life with Tornado by A.S. King' rel='nofollow noopener'>Still Life with Tornado</a> and I haven't the faintest frick what was going on in either of those. This is a bit more of a straight-forward book (except how she apologised to every pickle she ate in case it was her dead friend???????? i am so confused) and mostly was about <b>how we ignore things that are too difficult to face.</b> It's actually a really hard-hitting topic because I mean, who isn</span>
  <span id="freeText5090698884079999925" style="display:none"><b>I am a little confused! But also a little bit pleased with this one!</b> I confess I've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23203744.I_Crawl_Through_It" title="I Crawl Through It by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">I Crawl Through It</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28588459.Still_Life_with_Tornado" title="Still Life with Tornado by A.S. King" rel="nofollow noopener">Still Life with Tornado</a> and I haven't the faintest frick what was going on in either of those. This is a bit more of a straight-forward book (except how she apologised to every pickle she ate in case it was her dead friend???????? i am so confused) and mostly was about <b>how we ignore things that are too difficult to face.</b> It's actually a really hard-hitting topic because I mean, who isn't guilty of this? <br /><br />I definitely felt emotional a couple of times, like, gah, Charlie's life was just falling apart and so was Vera's, but she found a way (also having a loving dad helped) to stay on track, while Charlie just spiralled out of control.<br /><br /><b>Although ultimately:</b> (a) I am still kind of confused about so many things, and (b) I wish the secondary character, Charlie, had narrated instead of Vera. ¯\_(ツ)_/¯</span>

<div id="review_1352905389" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1352905389" />
    <a title="Anne " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23304719-anne"><img alt="Anne " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564193777p2/23304719.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1352905389?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne " href="/user/show/23304719-anne">Anne </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23304719-anne?shelf=5-star-books">5-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23304719-anne?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23304719-anne?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23304719-anne?shelf=self-discovery">self-discovery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1352905389" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14251632403636459303"><b>Rule number one: Don't fall in love with your best friend.</b><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457432217ra/18357337.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Oh please. Next you're going to tell me to control how the blood flows in my body.<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>Here’s me using tandem in a sentence.<br/> We will learn to forgive ourselves in tandem. </blockquote>
</i><br/>I know I said I was ready, and it would be a privilege to have my heart broken by this book. But did you ever wonder about it? About all the pieces of you you leave behind with every book you read and every page you turn. That oxymoronic feeling of being fully empty. And </span>
  <span id="freeText14251632403636459303" style="display:none"><b>Rule number one: Don't fall in love with your best friend.</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457432217ra/18357337.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Oh please. Next you're going to tell me to control how the blood flows in my body.<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>Here’s me using tandem in a sentence.<br> We will learn to forgive ourselves in tandem. </blockquote>
</i><br>I know I said I was ready, and it would be a privilege to have my heart broken by this book. But did you ever wonder about it? About all the pieces of you you leave behind with every book you read and every page you turn. That oxymoronic feeling of being fully empty. And that brings you back to acknowledging all the things you gained while being drained. I'm a dictionary of words I can't make sense of right now. God help me, words can't save me now.<br><br>⏩ <b>
  <u>
    <i>THERE'S JUST NO BETTER WAY THIS STORY COULD HAVE BEEN PRESENTED</i>
  </u>
</b><br><b>Please Ignore Vera Dietz is a lesson about speaking the truth.</b> About the tipsy balance between three variables of a deadly equation: action, inaction and reaction.<br>I'm sorry. I don't have fine literary sounding words for what I have to say next: We all know this simple truth. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457432217ra/18357338.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Landon knows it. I know it. You know it.<br>This book was blessed by the heavens and whatever celestial bodies are in charge of bookish extraordinariness. All the topics it circles around are so thought-provoking.<br><br>The story opens up with the ultimate question: <b>What happened on the night Charlie Kahn died?</b><br><br> The narration is given in first person narrative, with inputs from several characters(Vera's father - Ken, The pagoda - the inanimate narrator, The Dead Kid - Charlie himself) throughout the course of the story, but the character who invests more of her voice into the knitting of the story together, while simultaneously building up the mystery behind the death of Charlie Kahn is<b> Vera. </b> The narration is simply a mingling of past and present. I just can't tell you how much I loved Vera, I can't tell you how proud I am of her, and I can't tell you how much I hated her. I can't tell you how much I love-hated Charlie and all the characters in this book. Which leads me to:<br><br>⏩ <b>
  <u>
    <i>SOMEONE PLEASE EXPLAIN THE CHEMISTRY BEHIND FEELING BOTH HATRED AND LOVE FOR A PERSON AND WITH EQUAL PASSIONS TOO.</i>
  </u>
</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421881699ra/13425712.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>The first thing we find out about Vera and Charlie is Vera hates Charlie not just for dying, but for "screwing her over" and then dying. Leaving her to handle the mess he left behind. But before the hatred, she felt love. And even when she hated him, she still loved him.<b> We the Readers</b> get to tap into this minefield of contradiction. You want to scream out your hatred for Charlie, but at the same time you want to hug him. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1382817128ra/6221163.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>Please Ignore Vera is a home for all things cutting:</b> secrets and lies, truth and history, death and coping,<b> love and hatred,</b> <b>drugs and alcoholism, violence and abuse. And fate. </b>Yes that nasty booger came up again in here. He's just going around ruining people's lives, making them believe they can never outrun him, never leave him behind. Liar. The problem with truth is truth is everything we <b>believe.</b> The problem with choices is they're like double-edged swords. But believe it or not, we're all in an infinite, incognizant war with fate. Let's keep fighting. Charlie and Vera were so stupid to believe fate. So stupid. And when destiny/fate and whatever liar names he goes by is done messing with them, that's when they realize how easy it all was. How uncomplicated their whole lives could've been. And aren't we all the same? Hunched over and screaming out to the universe: Please. Let me have a do over! Just this once. Help me rewrite that ending.<br>Welcome to the eternal silence.<br><br>❎ <b>
  <i>
    <u>TWO SCENES THAT ABSOLUTELY CRUSHED ME AND SENT MY ASHES FLOATING THROUGH THE UNIVERSE</u>
  </i>
</b><br>⚫ <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ THE PUKE. THE FREAKING PUKE. How stupid. How stupidly sad and silly. I don't know how I kept on reading after that revelation. All the while I kept thinking it was something huge, the reason for Charlie's death was a big bulldozing matter. To find out it was something as silly as puke hurt me, it was like an extra coating of sadness. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>⚫ <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ WHEN CHARLIE BECAME HIS FATHER AND HIT VERA. <b>I. JUST. CAN'T.</b> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>⏩ <b>
  <u>
    <i>THE PROBLEM OF "JUST IGNORING IT"</i>
  </u>
</b><br>❎ The subject of domestic violence is not one to broach lightly, because from all accounts, it's not just about the problem of the abuser being abusive, it's more about the attitude of the abused. And It's not just the body that's battered, it's the mind. Under the weight of continuous abuse is where such simple and guiltless survival traits like adaptation and conditioned reflex become a curse. Remember to go rigid and assume your subservient pose in readiness for all possible physical altercations. Remember to flinch when the hand goes up, tighten your muscles, protect the delicate parts as that hand finally makes it's descent. Don't forget the face paints and powders and concealers. Remember to subconsciously settle into a life of alternating tolerance and justification of "well deserved punishments" because after a long time of coping, there's just no other way to live. It's so freaking ugly. Succumbing to mind and body control. But only you can get it all back. It's one point this book tried to make clear: <b>In the end only you can save yourself</b>. But at the same time, <u>support and help are crucial</u>. They are needed. Sealed lips don't make for cleaner wounds, ugly scars maybe. It's not going to go away or magically work out.<br><br>❎ Highschool is a secret world parents are barred from having access to. I begin to understand how hideously painful and nerve-racking it is to know your kid has secrets they can't share with you. I, for one, know my parents weren't stupid or blind to everything I tried to hide or hid from them. Parents, like Vera's dad might not know what exactly, but they do know something's up. It's funny, but this story made me realize, really, that parents can only do so much. They're guides and compasses, but at the end of the day they can't double as carvers and sculptors. So when kids run on wrong side of the road after all your worn out lessons of morality and responsibility, what then? Some say you keep trying, keep pushing. Some say it's just a rite of passage. The order of the business: Let them make their mistakes. Let them find their way. I'll be there every step of the way, and if they ever do decide to reach out, I'm going to meet them half way.<br> Don't ask me, I don't know. I'm no parent. I can only tell you about all the things I was grateful for as a kid.<br><br>⏩ <b>
  <u>
    <i> JENNY IS A FREAKING SHE DEVIL. IF YOU SEE HER COMING YOUR WAY RUN THE OTHER WAY. OR GRAB AN AXE.</i>
  </u>
</b><br>You're not convinced? Here's what she's described as at one point: <i>The way she stood there, like a character in a Stephen King novel, she was capable of anything. </i><br><br>If you've ever read a Stephen King novel you'll know that's some messed up shit right there. Jenny's character screams mental disorder. But this book passes Jenny off as the archetypical gum popping, hair grabbing, skanky, boy shagging, lying, pedestal hugging mean girl harassing the hallways of your highschool. I was oddly fascinated by her character. How could someone be so young and crazy? What kind of wrong wires could be touching in their head to turn them so dark, evil and spiteful? I'm confused about whether I should feel disgust or sympathy right now. The contrasting characters of Jenny and Vera was something that stood out for me. Ultimately, I identified with Vera. Of course. Her desire to just be ignored, to blend in and become one with the background, that's something I can understand. That's something most people can understand. Sure, some detest invisibility, but NO ONE wants to be noticed or marked for the wrong reasons in highschool. We all know highschool is a world of labels and hierarchical infrastructures. All the smart kids don't hang around looking for trouble when the bell goes out. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457432217ra/18357339.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Sadly, trouble seems to find some. That place is a jungle, I swear. If you made it out alive, be glad. And don't worry about your scars, I don't think anyone really leaves that world unscathed. I know some people claim bullies are more complex than the fists they throw around. I don't know about that. But I do know insecurity is a disease, and Jenny oozed it. Pity that. I've decided to be disgusted by her character. And if words are not enough, I could write a full review of gifery about all the ways Jenny was abhorrent. Stahp Jenny. Just Stahp speaking and existing or else<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457432217ra/18357340.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457432217ra/18357341.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457432217ra/18357342.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457432217ra/18357343.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457432217ra/18357344.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>✔ <b>One more question this book proffered:</b> the question of life outside the confining walls of high school. We can be anything once we exit those doors, but then again, sometimes we find out we're nothing. <b>Bill Corso</b> anybody?<br><br>⏩ <b>
  <u>
    <i>THE ENDING: GO OUT WITH A BANG.</i>
  </u>
</b><br>Rather than exit with an aesthetically pleasing ending, you go out with a bang. Embrace the chaos, welcome the fear while ironing out the kinks of your jacked up life.<br><br><b>This is Vera. </b>This is the evolutionary heroine. This song describes the whole cycle. And I kept thinking of it while I was reading. I kept thinking this is Vera:<br><a href="https://m.youtube.com/watch?v=53GIADHxVzM" rel="nofollow noopener">She Used To Be Mine</a><br><br><i>It's not what I asked for<br> Sometimes life just slips in through a back door<br> And carves out a person and makes you believe it's all true<br> And now I've got you<br> And you're not what I asked for<br> If I'm honest, I know I would give it all back<br> For a chance to start over and rewrite an ending or two<br> For the girl that I knew<br><br>Who'll be reckless, just enough<br> Who'll get hurt, but who learns how to toughen up<br> When she's bruised and gets used by a man who can't love<br> And then she'll get stuck<br> And be scared of the life that's inside her<br> Growing stronger each day 'til it finally reminds her<br> To fight just a little, to bring back the fire in her eyes<br> That's been gone, but used to be mine<br> Used to be mine</i><br><br><b>The whole Jenny drama:</b><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=s8e45WHIduM" rel="nofollow noopener">Between the Lines by Sara Bareilles</a><br><br><b>
  <u>The Problem with "Ignoring it"</u>
</b><br><b>Somebody should have helped Charlie:</b><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=lrulQAZq7Y8" rel="nofollow noopener">Medicine by Daughter</a><br><br><b>Somebody should have helped Mrs. Kahn:</b><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=SdSCCwtNEjA" rel="nofollow noopener">Cherry Wine by Hozier</a><br><br><br><b>
  <u>
    <i>⏩ DO I REALLY NEED TO TELL YOU QUOTES?</i>
  </u>
</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>I’d rather feel something for real than pretend it’s not what it is. (Which Zen guy said, “If you want to drown, do not torture yourself with shallow water”?) <br><br>But there’s something about telling other people what to ignore that just doesn’t work for me. Especially things we shouldn’t be ignoring. Kid bullying you at school? Ignore him. Girl passing rumors? Ignore her. Eighth-grade teacher pinch your friend’s ass? Ignore it. Sexist geometry teacher says girls shouldn’t go to college because they will only ever pop out babies and get fat? Ignore him. Hear that a girl in your class is in abused by her stepfather and had to go to the clinic? Hear she’s bringing her mother’s pills to school and selling them to pay for it? Ignore. Ignore. Ignore. Mind your own business. Don’t make waves. Fly under the radar. It’s just one of those things, Vera.<br> I’m sorry, but I don’t get it. <br><br>No one living understands dying, and no matter what they dream up—from harps and heaven to pickles in Big Macs—they can’t prove a thing until they’re on this side. Which, if you can, you want to avoid until it’s really your time to go. You might want to leave some time to fall in love and have a family. Stay healthy so you can meet your grandchildren one day. I can guarantee you this: you do not want to die by asphyxiating on your own puke and get kicked out of a car onto your front lawn. <br><br>Plus, youth is judgmental. <br><br>I have my fingers on the switch, but have lived a lifetime ignoring the control I have over my own world. Today is different. On the night he died, Charlie said he left something for me. Today I’m going to find it. <br><br>When my mother was my age, she was just about to have me after I’d spent nine long months growing inside her. Now it’s my turn. I am going to birth myself. I am going to be a <br>better mother to me than she ever was. I’m going to stay faithful and stand up for myself. I am going to do more than send me fifty bucks on my birthday, and if I ever call myself on the phone, I’m going to act like I care, just a little, because I’m aware that I might need it. I will comb my own hair gently and never make myself get into bathwater that’s too hot. I am going to be the kind of mother who shows warmth. <br><br> A BRIEF WORD FROM THE PAGODA<br> Hey—the whole freaking world was built from delusional optimism and folly. What makes you so special? We’re all just making it up as we go along. No one really knows what they’re doing. Anyone who tells you otherwise is talking out of their butt. <br><br>The way she stood there, like a character in a Stephen King novel, she was capable of anything. <br><br> “You wish you knew more? Seriously. You don’t.” I think, And when you do, you’ll wish you didn’t. </blockquote>
</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="14251632403636459303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_192861325" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192861325" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192861325?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=made-me-cry">made-me-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2011">reviewed-in-2011</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=moments-of-great-frustration">moments-of-great-frustration</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=i-see-dead-people">i-see-dead-people</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=readalong">readalong</a>,
