        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192861325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4914448724682768407"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/><b>“Is it okay to hate a dead kid? Even if you loved him once? Even if he was my best friend? Is it okay to hate him for being dead?” </b><br/><br/>Please Ignore Vera Dietz is a story about a 18-year-old girl faced with the loss of her best friend.<br/>On one side, this novel is burdened with a scary amount of raw realism. It tells a story that hits too close to home, one that none of us want to hear. There are pedophiles, abusive husbands, drinking problems, runaway mothers and friends who break our hearts.</span>
  <span id="freeText4914448724682768407" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br /><b>“Is it okay to hate a dead kid? Even if you loved him once? Even if he was my best friend? Is it okay to hate him for being dead?” </b><br /><br />Please Ignore Vera Dietz is a story about a 18-year-old girl faced with the loss of her best friend.<br />On one side, this novel is burdened with a scary amount of raw realism. It tells a story that hits too close to home, one that none of us want to hear. There are pedophiles, abusive husbands, drinking problems, runaway mothers and friends who break our hearts. There's too much to handle at once, for Vera and for me. <br />Then there’s the other side that is as far from reality as can possibly be. The funny yet touching flow charts, talking pagodas, best friends turned into pickles and thousands of haunting ghosts serve as a soothing balm that helps heal the wounds made by the all-too-possible first side of the story. <br />For the most part, when those two sides collide, the result is great and stunningly original. However, the combination didn’t work so well for the ending. When it came time to resolve Vera's situation, I wanted King to choose one or the other, to either write an utterly realistic ending, or a completely absurd one. What she gave us felt like a cop out. But who am I to judge? My rating is a cop out as well. <br /><br />It was easy enough to blame my three readalong partners for my reluctance to write this review. All three of them did such an amazing job. Ms. Marr’s <a>deliciously funny and incredibly smart words</a>, Ms. Reynje’s <a> colorful world that never fails to pull my heartstrings</a> and Ms. Lisa’s <a>strong logic and astonishing insightfulness</a> would intimidate even the most creative minds. But the bigger truth is that I needed time to figure out exactly why I didn’t enjoy this book quite as much as they did, especially when I claim to be such a huge fan of literary realism. And it’s true. Balzac, Stendhal, Tolstoy and many others helped me become the person I am today. But the reality they described for me is in no way my reality. I can easily dive into it knowing that I’m untouchable. Vera’s story, however, happens in everyone’s back yard. It’s the almost tangible reality of it that I can’t handle. <br /><br />That doesn’t mean that I won’t recommend this book to anyone who will listen. I’ll probably reread it myself at some point. <br /><br />A big thanks to Lisa, Reynje and Shirley for this amazing adventure that became known as the Double Date readalong. Everything is fun when you’re around. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4914448724682768407" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_141885926" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/141885926" />
    <a title="Annalisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/542037-annalisa"><img alt="Annalisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226336540p2/542037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/141885926?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annalisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annalisa" href="/user/show/542037-annalisa">Annalisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Annalisa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/947145-janessa">Janessa</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=voice">voice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer141885926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10056904800249387918">Some 20 pages into the book I thought to myself, "I don't really care what this book is about and honestly the subject matter hasn't grabbed me yet, but I don't care. I would follow this girl anywhere." I love a good voice.<br/><br/>Vera is a high school senior grieving over her best friend's death, only at the time of his death, Charlie was her frenemy. It makes the grieving process a little harder when you hate and love the person at the same time, when you have so many unresolved issues that you'll nev</span>
  <span id="freeText10056904800249387918" style="display:none">Some 20 pages into the book I thought to myself, "I don't really care what this book is about and honestly the subject matter hasn't grabbed me yet, but I don't care. I would follow this girl anywhere." I love a good voice.<br /><br />Vera is a high school senior grieving over her best friend's death, only at the time of his death, Charlie was her frenemy. It makes the grieving process a little harder when you hate and love the person at the same time, when you have so many unresolved issues that you'll never get answers to. Throw that on top of an already complicated life with a father who expects everything from her to avoid the pitfalls of his own life and a mother who abandoned her and Vera has a lot of conflicting emotions and decisions caving in on her.<br /><br />As Vera tries to move on with her life, she can't quite get away from Charlie and the things that only she knows about his life and death. The story is weaved with her present life and the little tidbits of her past life she lets bleed into her consciousness. It isn't until she deals with the mess of her relationship with Charlie that we learn the circumstances of his betrayal. I cried for her. It is so hard to find characters in YA that are relatable and real and raw. Vera is definitely one of them.<br /><br />The book is also scattered with POVs from her father (Ken), from Charlie, and from the town pagoda who's been around long enough to see pitfalls of the human condition. At first I wasn't sure how I felt about Ken's chapters (although I always loved his flow charts) but ended up liking that contrast of perspective very much. I could see where he was coming from and I could see where Vera was coming from and appreciate both sides of the argument. It added to the complexity of the story and the characters.<br /><br />The only thing that really bothered me was I didn't feel satisfied with the answers Charlie gave. He was a little bit of a drama queen about Vera helping him out but what he left as answers and explanations didn't quite add up to his level of anxiety. He had the opportunity for a grand gesture and it fell a little flat. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And I never quite understood how he died. He was hiding and then he was thrown from who knew whose moving car drunk. How did they find him? Why did he agree to hang out and get wasted? Why did he feel that he should be in jail? And what exactly was John the pervert doing? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />In the end I was satisfied with Vera's story and closed the book smiling. That is the best feeling at the end of a book. It wasn't all better in the end, a bandaid to cover the gaping whole in her heart, but it was about coping and growing into the person she wanted to be. Most importantly, I was left with a sense of hope, which is all I wanted for Vera in the first place.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10056904800249387918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_379898259" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/379898259" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/379898259?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer379898259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer953903733476021043">On the surface level, <i>Please Ignore Vera Dietz</i> is about the death of a girl's best friend. But, because that would be too easy, it's much deeper. Vera Dietz, the girl in question, has spent a solid portion of her life in love with Charlie Khan - the same boy she hung out with when she was a kid. Then high school happens, and their relationship takes a turn for the worse. Vera comes to hate Charlie; however, when Charlie dies in a devastating way, will she be willing to clear his name?<br/><br/><i>Please Igno</i></span>
  <span id="freeText953903733476021043" style="display:none">On the surface level, <i>Please Ignore Vera Dietz</i> is about the death of a girl's best friend. But, because that would be too easy, it's much deeper. Vera Dietz, the girl in question, has spent a solid portion of her life in love with Charlie Khan - the same boy she hung out with when she was a kid. Then high school happens, and their relationship takes a turn for the worse. Vera comes to hate Charlie; however, when Charlie dies in a devastating way, will she be willing to clear his name?<br /><br /><i>Please Ignore Vera Dietz</i> isn't an easy read. It contains the death of a best friend, a mother who abandons her daughter, alcoholic genes, bullies, etc. One of the several unique aspects of A.S. King's novel is the contrast of those dark topics with the lighthearted and witty voice of Vera, the protagonist. I ascertained the struggle Vera went through, but it wasn't all that clear or well-defined; it wasn't "my best friend died, now I feel grief" but much more complex and intriguing.<br /><br />King accomplished many tasks with this work. She utilized various first-person perspectives (one of them is a pagoda), carried the mystery throughout the story, and presented numerous touchy issues without taking on a trite tone. Despite my three-star rating, I would recommend this book to teens because it contains little thought grenades that make you step back and reevaluate your life experiences.<br /><br />But for some reason I simply didn't love this book. Reading through other reviews on Goodreads from more seasoned/analytical perspectives makes me think that yes, this was a fantastic novel. Yet there's something - and perhaps this is an entirely personal conundrum - that prevents me from giving it the utmost praise. Maybe it's because I found the plot lines and characters dry (even if they were superbly original) or I just felt an unexplainable lack of empathy overall. Either way, I would recommend this one. It just didn't entirely resonate with me.<br /><br />*review cross-posted on my blog, <a href="http://thequietvoice18.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">the quiet voice</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="953903733476021043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

I think it's quirky without being corny and she did really well writing a teenager's voice. That being said, I thought the plot of this book lacked a little bit of direction. It wasn't reaaally a mystery, and it mainly jumped back and forth between past and present, which I typically don't enjoy but in this case, I was alright with it because the layout and writing was done so well. Vera was a</span>

I think it's quirky without being corny and she did really well writing a teenager's voice. That being said, I thought the plot of this book lacked a little bit of direction. It wasn't reaaally a mystery, and it mainly jumped back and forth between past and present, which I typically don't enjoy but in this case, I was alright with it because the layout and writing was done so well. Vera was awesome, nevertheless, and this book had a depth to it in the end that I wasn't expecting.</span>

<div id="review_749802686" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/749802686" />
    <a title="Mari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14524726-mari"><img alt="Mari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534621204p2/14524726.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/749802686?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mari" href="/user/show/14524726-mari">Mari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14524726-mari?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14524726-mari?shelf=read-in-english">read-in-english</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer749802686" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9415985381866184464"><br/><b>1.5/5</b><br/><br/>Yes, please, ignore Vera Dietz. Ignore this book altogether.<br/><br/>At first I thought it was just too off-the-wall-quirky for my liking. Which it was. But so much worse than that, too.<br/><br/>Meet Vera. She's better than you. And everyone else tbh.<br/><br/>According to her.<br/><br/><u>Important</u>: Vera is not a slut. Cause there are a lot of sluts in this book. You are a stripper? You are a slut. You wear black eyeliner? You are a slut. You enjoy cheerleading and college sports? You are a slut. And sucking dicks is probs one of</span>
  <span id="freeText9415985381866184464" style="display:none"><br /><b>1.5/5</b><br /><br />Yes, please, ignore Vera Dietz. Ignore this book altogether.<br /><br />At first I thought it was just too off-the-wall-quirky for my liking. Which it was. But so much worse than that, too.<br /><br />Meet Vera. She's better than you. And everyone else tbh.<br /><br />According to her.<br /><br /><u>Important</u>: Vera is not a slut. Cause there are a lot of sluts in this book. You are a stripper? You are a slut. You wear black eyeliner? You are a slut. You enjoy cheerleading and college sports? You are a slut. And sucking dicks is probs one of your hobbies. You date boys? SLUT. Don't deny it - Vera knows. Vera is not a slut, though. Everyone else is a slut. This is a book about Vera vs. sluts. Sluts and all things slutty. Did I tell you there's lots of slutty stuff about sluts in here? Go ask Vera.<br /><br />(Though I guess we <i>are</i> supposed to be outraged by this whole "everyone's a slut" business. Maybe we're supposed to see this book as some kind of painfully realistic tale, told by an overly honest narrator. After all, here's how Vera's best friend describes her: "You should go back and be yourself. Cynical, funny, straight-up Vera Dietz." Is that it? Well, if it is, then up until now I didn't know "cynical" and "funny" meant obnoxious and detestable, which is all Vera is.)<br /><br />Be sure you can locate Florida on a map, or else you and Vera won't be friends. She's too intellectually advanced for your shit.<br /><br />Be sure you're able to read, too, cause if you're not, Vera might just go and make fun of you. Then complain about you being a dick to her.<br /><br />Avoid being Mexican, because you'll encounter such gems:<br /><blockquote>"I drive over the bridge into town. The whitest town on Earth - or, more accurately, once the whitest town on Earth until the Mexicans moved in. Once you get through the crowded old suburbs where the large Victorian homes sit on the hill and past the rows of cupola-topped row houses, it’s an ugly town - a mishmash of 1940s asphalt shingles, multicolored bricks, and gray concrete. There’s too much litter, and too many people look angry. Dad says it wasn’t always like this. He says it’s not the Mexicans’ fault that the city council would rather spend the city’s money on new arts initiatives and a big, flashy baseball stadium than more police on the streets. So now, while there’s wine, cheese, and doubleheaders downtown, poverty has taken over and crime is at an all-time high uptown."</blockquote>But it's okay, cause <i>Vera's dad</i> said that "it's not the Mexicans' fault". It's just that, one is left wondering about what <i>the author</i> meant to tell us here. Or maybe, y'know... "Painfully realistic tale" and the whole shebang? No thanks.<br /><br />You'll also meet <i>"Nathan (Nate) [...] a six-foot-five black guy,"</i> who wears a <i>"hokey MC Hammer leather coat"</i> and greets people like: <i>"Yo, [Vera]! What’s shakin’?"</i> (yes, that's an actual quote.) But he only pops-up once, in the beginning of the book, then disappears mysteriously.<br /><br />Oh, but don't get sad. Cause there's Mick, at your service.<br /><blockquote>"I’m even growing to like Mick, the skinhead Nazi. He tells funny jokes and has a very witty way about him. [...] Mick walks over to me with his arms out, as if he wants to hug me, and I flinch into James’s side. I do not want to hug a skinhead Nazi. Even if he might be okay. Even if he tells funny jokes. <b>Even if he’s really just a misunderstood nice guy who hates certain races of people.</b>"</blockquote>And let's not forget about Jenny, the bad girl who wears lots of black eyeliner (SLUTTY), who stole Vera's best friend/crush, dresses in all black, and hurts puppies. I wish I were joking about the puppies...<br /><br />Jenny is mean. Mean for the sake of it. Sometimes you just need one of them mean sluts with no depth at all to make your book woth it, y'know...<br /><br />Random quotes because of reasons:<br /><blockquote>"He’s so awesomely gorgeous and manly and hunky. His hair is grown out a little, so he doesn’t look messy, but rugged. He keeps himself shaven, but sometimes leaves a stubbly goatee, which he’s done today. He wears a Pagoda shirt that’s a tiny bit small for him, so his biceps and deltoids are really defined and I can’t help but want to squeeze them. But this isn’t all physical. He says smart stuff. He’s funny, sarcastic, and cynical. He can see outside this stupid little town because he’s been out of this stupid little town. None of the guys in school have all this going for them. They might have muscles, but they don’t have brains. Or they might have muscles and a few brains, but they still think the world revolves around them."</blockquote>NO, this isn't all physical, cause that would be slutty! Vera isn't slutty! Never forget! *holds lighter in the air*. "[...] but they still think the world revolves around them" ...and obviously it doesn't, since it already revolves around Vera. I mean c'mon.<br /><br /><blockquote>"He looks at me and smiles. 'You want to go out after work?'<br />'Where to?'<br /><b>'How about we go up to the pagoda and make out?'</b><br />This makes me so happy, I whistle while I do the dishes."</blockquote>1) That's... straightforward? (Dude's not her boyfriend or anything. They kissed once, it was awkward -according to Vera- and she didn't know how to talk to him or look at him afterwards. Then this happens. Just giving you a context, bye.) 2) VERA NO. THIS IS SLUTTY. VERA WHAT ARE YOU DOING??! VERA!! SAVE VERA FROM SLUTHOOD 2K14!!!<br /><br /><blockquote>"There was no doubt Mr. Oberman was gay. He didn’t hide it. I’d venture a guess that he was overly gay in the detention room because it irked the Detentionheads so much. Bill Corso was not going to be told what to do by some fag - so Oberman put on his extra fagginess just to make kids like Corso squirm."</blockquote>I MEAN??????????????? No amount of "painfully realistic tale, told by an overly honest narrator" bullshit will make me go, "Ahhh, this is a delightful read indeed."<br /><br />Charlie's story was... sad? His life (I didn't finish the book, so I have no idea how he died) kinda was, at the very least. But -and I feel terrible for saying this, I do- I just couldn't bring myself to like him much. He was supposed to be one of the main characters, but felt more like a a completely pointless one, added only to praise Vera for her greatness. Whenever we got chapters written from his PoV ("A brief word from the dead kid"), that was the only thing he did: PRAISE. FUCKING. VERA. Which did NOT make me feel like they had a connection or some true feelings, platonic or otherwise, for each other. The only effect it managed to have on me was irritate me. (Note: Authors! Don't <i>tell</i> me how awesome someone is! Show me! Make them <i>act</i> awesome! Repeating page after page after page that someone's oh-so-cool-you-have-no-idea-ohmigod won't make me think they are!) Not to mention that there was absolutely nothing to praise. She's been horrible to him. Why they were best friends is a mystery to me.<br /><br />And then he'd say stuff like this about his parents:<br /><blockquote>"I spend most of my time watching my parents <i>(from where he is now, the afterlife or something)</i>. You’d think I’d get as far away from them as I could now that I’m free, but seems I’m here to learn something. Not sure what. I never liked either of them. He’s just a bully, and she’s a doormat."</blockquote>Why am i shocked? His father is abusive. Crazy abusive. Woman-i-don't-want-you-to-use-tampons-because-it's-like-you're-cheating-on-me crazy abusive. And what does Charlie call him? A "bully". And his mother is a "doormat". Need I say more?<br /><br />Now, I don't know, maybe she never protected him and he's angry and that's why he doesn't care about her. But he doesn't express anger. He's just calling her... well, a doormat. Because "Ugh you so have no character and let your husband beat you."<br /><br />Because, you see, I do not mind characters thinking and doing stuff that's ethically wrong... as long as the author makes it clear that it IS ethically wrong and that the character is being a dick. I've never gotten that vibe from this book, ever.<br /><br />And Vera, I just............................................... I have no snark left. This girl was infuckingsufferable. The worst best friend one could have. I don't even know what to say, she infuriates me. Reading the book from her PoV was a torture. <br /><br />The writing wasn't half bad, though. That's it, that's the only positive aspect of the book bye.<br /><br />-------------------------------<br /><br />Okay i have this book downloaded... I need to read it asap, because i just discovered that it's by the same author as "Everybody Sees the Ants" and i've wanted to read <i>that</i> book for months. But i didn't want to buy it because i was afraid i'd hate it and spend my money for nothing... The "Vera Dietz" one received a lot of good reviews, soooo...<br /></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375865640" href="/book/show/12305758-please-ignore-vera-dietz">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25309949-lotte?shelf=a-young-adult-fiction">a-young-adult-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1032174923" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13558420790302183651">4.25/5 stars! Oh, this was actually really good!<br/>I especially liked Vera's straight-forward narration and the way she didn't gloss over anything. She mentioned periods, tampons and swearing, and it all felt very real. All of the main characters in this book felt very tangible and real by the way. I loved the way the relationship between Vera and her father was described and the way family dynamics in general were handled in this book. This, too, felt very realistic. In 'real life', no one is inhe</span>
  <span id="freeText13558420790302183651" style="display:none">4.25/5 stars! Oh, this was actually really good!<br />I especially liked Vera's straight-forward narration and the way she didn't gloss over anything. She mentioned periods, tampons and swearing, and it all felt very real. All of the main characters in this book felt very tangible and real by the way. I loved the way the relationship between Vera and her father was described and the way family dynamics in general were handled in this book. This, too, felt very realistic. In 'real life', no one is inherently good or evil, everyone has their flaws and their issues and A.S. King seemed to emphasize this in her book. The writing also flowed very easily and I appreciated how quick I was able to finish this, since I read this alongside two books for uni, which I'm having such a hard time getting through.<br />The 'mystery' in the story itself wasn't really a mystery though and I have to admit that I was slightly disappointed by that. I also would've loved to get a deeper look into Jenny Flick's life. Why did she act the way she did?<br />I'm so glad I already have another A.S. King book on my shelves, because I can't wait to pick up more books by her!</span>
  <a data-text-id="13558420790302183651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_267000896" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/267000896" />
    <a title="Lora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4632071-lora"><img alt="Lora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305237530p2/4632071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/267000896?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lora" href="/user/show/4632071-lora">Lora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of YA realistic fiction</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lora by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3222236-reut">Reut</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=lib-read">lib-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=g-ya-realistic">g-ya-realistic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer267000896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17862751362572177968"><b>
  <i>Is it okay to hate a dead kid? Even if I loved him once? Even if he was my best friend? Is it okay to hate him for being dead?</i>
</b><br/><br/>Vera's conflicting feelings toward Charlie after his death mirror mine over her story. I don't think I've ever been this conflicted over a book in all my years of reading.<br/><br/>Vera Dietz has secrets: she has a crush on a boy five years her senior; she's drinking vodka coolers under the radar; and, perhaps her biggest secret of all, she knows a whole helluva lot more about </span>
  <span id="freeText17862751362572177968" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Is it okay to hate a dead kid? Even if I loved him once? Even if he was my best friend? Is it okay to hate him for being dead?</i>
</b><br /><br />Vera's conflicting feelings toward Charlie after his death mirror mine over her story. I don't think I've ever been this conflicted over a book in all my years of reading.<br /><br />Vera Dietz has secrets: she has a crush on a boy five years her senior; she's drinking vodka coolers under the radar; and, perhaps her biggest secret of all, she knows a whole helluva lot more about her best friend's death than she's letting anyone in on. But she has her reasons: after you lose the boy you could've/should've been more than friends with, what else are you left with but to move on with someone else? And everyone knows alcohol is the perfect desensitizer when the pain is just too much. And besides, if she told anyone — her father, her classmates, the authorities — what might happen then?<br /><br />Much like its main character, <i>Please Ignore Vera Dietz</i> was, for me, all of the following: baffling, annoying, infuriating, wondrous, a true eye-opener. On the one side I think, if a book can make me feel so many conflicting emotions, shouldn't it be worth five stars? You know, just because, unlike so many books, it made me <i>feel</i>? And on the other, shouldn't I have felt more for the characters and their heartache and tough situation <b>before</b> the near-end mark? Somehow I think this would be easier if I didn't have to rate this, because, no matter what I put in those line of stars, they won't truly represent my feelings towards this particular work. I feel like this book is worth five stars and about two and a half all at once.<br /><br />I suppose the only way to give some semblance of order to this review is to break my thoughts down in a positive/negative fashion:<br /><br />NEGATIVE:<br /><br />Vera, Vera, Vera. What to say about this girl? Unlike any character (female or otherwise) I've ever read about, Vera Dietz made me, at some points, mad as hell; and at others, sad to the same degree. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I couldn't figure out why she didn't just call the police and keep the pet store from burning in the first place. Would that have been so hard? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> She is strange and quirky, and not exactly in a good way: she eats napkins just because Charlie did; she drinks and starts going out with a twenty-three-year-old guy, all while thinking of how much she <i>doesn't</i> want to end up like her father and mother, a recovered alcoholic and ex-stripper turned child-abandoner, respectively. I know people do stupid things when they're hurt, especially when they've recently lost someone they loved. They may even be entitled to do these things, but that doesn't make them interesting to read about or make a character endearing or worthy of my sympathy. Or at least it doesn't for me, anyway.<br />It wasn't until certain things happened and certain things were revealed that I started to feel something for her character, started to connect with her in any way. This happened much later in the story and, by then, it was (almost) too little too late.<br /><br />POSITIVE:<br /><br />When I <i>did</i> finally start to get it, finally began to see what so many people are raving about, it really hit hard. One minute I was reading along, thinking how this book just isn't for me but I'll finish it anyway, and the next I'm grabbing tissues to blot my tears before they left crinkle stains on my library's copy. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This, of course, happened when Vera relates the time Charlie threw dog shit on her in the forest. I couldn't believe that they were such close friends, to the point where they had fallen in love with each other, and yet he'd do something so humilating and disgusting to her. I felt for Vera in that moment. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The best part of this story is Vera's reconnecting with her father and rebuilding a real relationship with him. If you've read any of my past reviews, you know I appreciate good parent/child relationships more than any romance. Romances are nice, but they aren't everything. People say that romantic relationships can die but friends last forever, and I disagree. I'm more of a blood-runs-thicker-than-water kind of gal.<br />Friendships are wonderful, don't get me wrong. But let's face it: the right (wrong) thing happens, and that's it, no more BFF. I believe that <b>familial</b> relationships are the most important, the kind you can count on the most. And this is why they are, essentially, my favorite sort of relationship to read about. Vera and her father have many things to work out, including Vera's apparent use of alcohol to cope with the loss of Charlie and her father having never truly gotten over her mother when she left them. Their scenes together were some of my favorite.<br /><br />King's writing is edgy, sparse and peppered with wry humor. It made the pages flip fast and kept me invested in the story, even when the characters couldn't.<br /><br />As you can see, I'm very conflicted on this particular novel. I went into it thinking it would be an easy five stars, and ended up being disappointed on multiple accounts. Perhaps some day I'll return to this story, revisit its characters and maybe see them in the same light others have. Until then, <i>Please Ignore Vera Dietz</i> is a story that touched me at times, and frustrated me at others. But I feel better for having read it and I have no regrets. <b>3.5 stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17862751362572177968" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_115821245" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/115821245" />
    <a title="Mark" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1274105-mark"><img alt="Mark" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393119502p2/1274105.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/115821245?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mark" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mark" href="/user/show/1274105-mark">Mark</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1274105-mark?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1274105-mark?shelf=engl-492-spring-2012">engl-492-spring-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1274105-mark?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1274105-mark?shelf=relationships">relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1274105-mark?shelf=death-and-dying">death-and-dying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1274105-mark?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1274105-mark?shelf=engl-492-spring-2013">engl-492-spring-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1274105-mark?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1274105-mark?shelf=engl-492-spring-2011">engl-492-spring-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1274105-mark?shelf=mature-readers">mature-readers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer115821245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2765357975633523969">"It's one thing if he wants to ignore it. I guess that's fine. I mean, I ignore plenty of stuff, like school spirit days and the dirty looks I get from the Detentionheads while I try to slink through the halls unnoticed. But there's something about telling other people what to ignore that just doesn't work for me. Especially things we shouldn't be ignoring.<br/><br/>Kid bullying you at school? Ignore him. Girl passing rumors? Ignore her. Eighth grade teacher pinch your friend's ass? Ignore it. Sexist geom</span>
  <span id="freeText2765357975633523969" style="display:none">"It's one thing if he wants to ignore it. I guess that's fine. I mean, I ignore plenty of stuff, like school spirit days and the dirty looks I get from the Detentionheads while I try to slink through the halls unnoticed. But there's something about telling other people what to ignore that just doesn't work for me. Especially things we shouldn't be ignoring.<br /><br />Kid bullying you at school? Ignore him. Girl passing rumors? Ignore her. Eighth grade teacher pinch your friend's ass? Ignore it. Sexist geometry teacher says girls shouldn't go to college because they will only ever pop out babies and get fat? Ignore him. Hear that a girl in my class is being abused by her stepfather and had to go to the clinic? Hear she's bringing her mother's pills to school and selling them to pay for it? Ignore, ignore, ignore. Mind your own business. Don't make waves. Fly under the radar. It's just one of those things, Vera.<br /><br />I'm sorry, but I don't get it. If we're supposed to ignore everything that's wrong with our lives, then I can't see how we'll ever make things right."<br /><br />I'm so glad I assigned this book for my class, again; great excuse to re-read it, and I find something new within it each time I read it. And that's the mark of a great book, for me. <br /><br />Original review: <br /><br />Wow. With my schedule, I usually can't read books in a day, but I could not put this one aside for more than a few minutes at a time. This book is absolutely extraordinary, and I cannot wait to see it on "best of" lists after it's release this fall.<br /><br />Vera Dietz is an 18 year-old "pizza delivery technician," moving through her senior year of high school while living with her father (Vera's mother left some years prior). Vera's best friend since age 4, Charlie, died at the end of the summer, and Vera has been dealing with Charlie's death, but also the way he hurt her in the months leading up to his passing. The changes that came over Charlie, and the way he can still communicate with Vera from beyond the grave, move her to disclose important information about what happened on the night Charlie died, information that can clear his name, and perhaps give Vera some peace.<br /><br />A synopsis cannot do justice to this book. I will admit some bias, because the story takes place in my hometown (or a suspiciously close replica), and I enjoyed noticing the little name-changes that King used to represent real streets, schools, etc. And the inclusion of the Reading, PA, Pagoda in a YA novel, even giving it a voice in the story, has just about made my year.<br /><br />That being said, Vera is one of the most powerful female characters I've read in a while. She's completely messed up by her parents' divorce (Charlie has even greater issues with his parents), and she's an honest, vulnerable portrait of a teenager who is simply drifting through her life - working, going to school, dating - while letting the events of her life crash over her like cascading waves. Her voice is smart, funny and sarcastic, and the novel has enough surprises to leave readers guessing about Charlie's fate up until the end. <br /><br />Five stars were not enough for this book; I loved it that much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2765357975633523969" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_159972456" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159972456" />
    <a title="Pat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1026088-pat"><img alt="Pat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226920386p2/1026088.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/159972456?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pat" href="/user/show/1026088-pat">Pat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780375896170" href="/book/show/9476470-please-ignore-vera-dietz">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer159972456&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer159972456" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18078178717168812630">I finished this book though I wish I hadn't. <br/>There are qualities in the writing, the plot and the voice. The father, daughter relationship resolves beautifully in the end. Vera is a likable character a reader can root for. Yet, I am tired of the YA novel that focuses on depravity. Foul language, perversion, alcohol abuse, promiscuity are at the core secret of this story. <br/>I also had a problem with the depth of the "evil" character, the nemesis of the protagonist Vera. A seventeen year old girl wh</span>
  <span id="freeText18078178717168812630" style="display:none">I finished this book though I wish I hadn't. <br />There are qualities in the writing, the plot and the voice. The father, daughter relationship resolves beautifully in the end. Vera is a likable character a reader can root for. Yet, I am tired of the YA novel that focuses on depravity. Foul language, perversion, alcohol abuse, promiscuity are at the core secret of this story. <br />I also had a problem with the depth of the "evil" character, the nemesis of the protagonist Vera. A seventeen year old girl who kills her boyfriend because he breaks up with her? A girl who soaks the pet store with gasoline and sets it on fire? A girl and her circle of friends whose cruelty is incomprehensible? I'm sure somewhere out there are depraved teenagers but please....they must be the anomaly. In this novel, they are the norm.<br />I wish I'd read the jacket and not trusted the Printz award for excellence in young adult lit. The jacket warns that it is dark and surprising. I feel like I need to take out my brain and give it a shower after this read.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18078178717168812630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375865640" href="/book/show/12305758-please-ignore-vera-dietz">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21372390-wayne-barrett?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1274909059" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2733023673535410851"><br/>This is my second A.S King novel: Everybody Sees The Ants, and now, Please Ignore Vera Dietz. Lets just say, I have already added a couple more of her books. <br/><br/>The two aforementioned that I have read and the two that I have added are listed as YA novels. I can agree with this genre labeling because they deal with the lives of young adults, but the stories and the writing are such that, even as an older man, I found entertaining, gripping and pleasing due to the writing style of A.S. King.<br/><br/>Please Ig</span>
  <span id="freeText2733023673535410851" style="display:none"><br />This is my second A.S King novel: Everybody Sees The Ants, and now, Please Ignore Vera Dietz. Lets just say, I have already added a couple more of her books. <br /><br />The two aforementioned that I have read and the two that I have added are listed as YA novels. I can agree with this genre labeling because they deal with the lives of young adults, but the stories and the writing are such that, even as an older man, I found entertaining, gripping and pleasing due to the writing style of A.S. King.<br /><br />Please Ignore Vera Dietz is a coming of age tale that deals with some pretty big issues concerning loss and abandonment. There are issues of bullying and peer pressure. There are points of addictions and the ignorance of bliss. All in all this was a powerful but easy novel to read. This is one I would feel comfortable in recommending to all of my friends. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_157199245" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/157199245" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2467655-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596119990p2/2467655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/157199245?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/2467655-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer157199245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5968027655713588126"><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br/>Ahhh. Everything is going to be OK. <br/><br/><b>High point.</b><br/>OK, I tried to just pick one, but I couldn't narrow it down to just one in this case. I LOVED LOVED LOVED THIS BOOK. But anyway- Vera Dietz, one of the most realistic (and likeable) heroines I have ever read, such a compelling story, AS Kings' writing is just ridiculously engaging and I honestly couldn't put it down, well-thought out characters (even the secondary ones), BEST DAD EVER, heart-breakingly honest, FLOW CHARTS</span>
  <span id="freeText5968027655713588126" style="display:none"><b>Initial Final Page Thoughts.</b><br />Ahhh. Everything is going to be OK. <br /><br /><b>High point.</b><br />OK, I tried to just pick one, but I couldn't narrow it down to just one in this case. I LOVED LOVED LOVED THIS BOOK. But anyway- Vera Dietz, one of the most realistic (and likeable) heroines I have ever read, such a compelling story, AS Kings' writing is just ridiculously engaging and I honestly couldn't put it down, well-thought out characters (even the secondary ones), BEST DAD EVER, heart-breakingly honest, FLOW CHARTS and finally, I loved how it was told from different perspectives (even inanimate buildings!)<br /><b>
  <br />
</b><br /><b>Low Point.</b><br />GODDAMMIT CHARLIE, WHY ARE YOU DEAD?!<br /><br /><b>Heroine.</b><br />I feel I need to create a new award for Ms Dietz. <b>The Vera Dietz Soul Sister Prize</b>. She is just so awesome and fiesty and real and honest and perfect and I like to think that we would be friends if we went to the same high school. We would eat Big Macs (and she could have all my pickles because I don't like them!) and bitch about the bitchy bitch slag that is Jenny Flick. Seriously, why can't all heroines be like this? SORT IT, AUTHORS.<br /><br /><b>Love Interest.</b><br />Oh Charlie Khan. You weird one. You treat my soul sister like crap but I'm still rooting for you to get together with her. And then I remember you're dead and my heart is broken and it's not pretty. Thank you, AS King. You write the cutest scenes ever and make me wish I had had a sort of mentally unstable lovecrush when I was 16 who encouraged me to eat napkins and throw paper aeroplanes and then after a few of heart-fluttering moments be like 'Mmm.. yeah, CK is dead and this lovely thing between him and Vera? Yeah, it's not happening. Nor will it EVER.' Gutpunch.<br /><br /><b>Baddie.</b><br />Ugh, Jenny Flick. I went to an all girls school so I knew lots of people like her (not to the same mental state as JF, but definitely the same needless maliciousness that only teenage girls know how to execute to make people's lives hell). The combination of Jenny Flick and Vera just shows how perfectly AS King understands teenagers, especially girls. Even though I hate hate hate her, she is a great character.<br /><br /><b>Angst Scale.</b><br />6/10.<br />Even though death is one of the major subject of the book, it is not what it is all about. Vera isn’t sure how she feels about Charlie’s death because she wasn’t sure how she felt about Charlie. I have given it a relatively low score on the angst scale because Vera is very mature and downplays the grief that is bubbling below the surface. Really effective. Also, the relationship between Vera and her Dad is just perfect, especially because we get a few chapters from his perspective. Jenny Flick may cause angst… but she’s a bitch and isn’t even worth bothering over.<br /><b>
  <br />
</b><br /><b>Recommended for.</b><br /><i>
  <u>EVERYONE</u>
</i>. People who like interesting and complex stories. People who want to read books that are set in the now. People who like convincing teen speak and not all ‘LOL’ and ‘LMAO’. People who love strong female mcs. People who like books that aren’t all about romance and lurrrve. Or if you are... realistic love that reminds you of summer days sitting with friends when you're supposed to be doing a million different things. People who like Big Macs…and pizza.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5968027655713588126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_151116896" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/151116896" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/151116896?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151116896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18131142374844688312">4 1/2 stars<br/><br/>I know that I really enjoyed this one because I kept sneaking off on the other two books that I’m currently reading to cheat with it. This enigmatic, clever story is told mainly by Vera Dietz, with guest spots for her dad, her recently dead best friend Charlie, and the Pagoda (an architectural oddity in her town). Vera’s very angry with Charlie at the beginning of this book, for reasons which the reader is slowly allowed to know through a series of flashbacks and hints. I don't want t</span>
  <span id="freeText18131142374844688312" style="display:none">4 1/2 stars<br /><br />I know that I really enjoyed this one because I kept sneaking off on the other two books that I’m currently reading to cheat with it. This enigmatic, clever story is told mainly by Vera Dietz, with guest spots for her dad, her recently dead best friend Charlie, and the Pagoda (an architectural oddity in her town). Vera’s very angry with Charlie at the beginning of this book, for reasons which the reader is slowly allowed to know through a series of flashbacks and hints. I don't want to reveal too much because I think that this book is better if you just fall into it and let everything happen.<br /><br />I really love the way that this story unfolded with snappy writing and brief provoking chapters. The style and humor really kept my attention through out. I am also just so impressed with how fully realized the characters are, especially given that one of the main characters is dead before the book even begins. This is one of my favorite passages from the book:<br /><br /><i>"Because with Charlie, nothing was ever easy. Everything was windswept and octagonal and finger-combed. Everything was difficult and odd, and the theme songs all had minor chords.”</i><br /><br />I love how she captures so much of Charlie’s character with so few words.<br /> <br />There are some really great messages tucked away in this book as well - such as, is it better to confront violence and abuse or avert your eyes? And, can you ever escape the time-bomb of your genetic inheritance? That one really hit me on a personal level. The one issue I have with this book (which is why I gave it four and a half stars instead of five) is a personal one as well. Having gone through the abandonment of a parent, it was hard for me to buy in to the seeming happiness and acceptance from Vera and her father at the end of this book. I know that my disbelief is simply the result of me being too jaded and negative on the subject, but still…I feel that it would take much more than four therapy sessions to have that level of acceptance from them. As a result, the happy ending left me feeling a bit disconnected. I really loved everything else about this book though – I highly recommend it!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18131142374844688312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1263371694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1263371694" />
    <a title="Anastasia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29194167-anastasia"><img alt="Anastasia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459611514p2/29194167.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1263371694?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anastasia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anastasia" href="/user/show/29194167-anastasia">Anastasia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8732024-please-ignore-vera-dietz">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1263371694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1110417257526945585"><b> 4/5 </b><br/><b> <i> Trigger Warning: death of a loved one </i></b>  <br/><br/>Please Ignore Vera Dietz is a heartbreaking book about love and loss.<br/><br/>Vera’s spent her whole life secretly in love with her best friend, Charlie Kahn. And over the years she’s kept a lot of his secrets. Even after he betrayed her. Even after he ruined everything.<br/>So when Charlie dies in dark circumstances, Vera knows a lot more than anyone—the kids at school, his family, even the police. But will she emerge to clear his name? Does she even want to?<br/><br/>I w</span>
  <span id="freeText1110417257526945585" style="display:none"><b> 4/5 </b><br /><b> <i> Trigger Warning: death of a loved one </i></b>  <br /><br />Please Ignore Vera Dietz is a heartbreaking book about love and loss.<br /><br />Vera’s spent her whole life secretly in love with her best friend, Charlie Kahn. And over the years she’s kept a lot of his secrets. Even after he betrayed her. Even after he ruined everything.<br />So when Charlie dies in dark circumstances, Vera knows a lot more than anyone—the kids at school, his family, even the police. But will she emerge to clear his name? Does she even want to?<br /><br />I went into this book with an average expectation. If it weren't for my friend I would've had very low expectations. Thank goodness she kept pestering me about reading it. This book is everything you want in a book that deals with teenage grief. <br /><br />Vera is angry. She's angry and alone. Her mother left her at age 12, her father is an accountant and human self help book that thinks ignoring the problem is the best solution, and her best friend and neighbor, Charlie, is dead. In the last few months of Charlie's life Vera and Charlie began to drift away. Rumors were spread and trust was broken.<br /><br /><blockquote> “Is it okay to hate a dead kid? Even if you loved him once? Even if he was my best friend? Is it okay to hate him for being dead?” </blockquote><br /><br />This book dealt with grief and loss flawlessly. It showed you how your emotions are valid even if they're grief, sorrow, anger, or happiness. No one can tell you when and how you should move on. The phrase "move on" is ignorant. No one ever <i> moves on </i>, we just cope. We live and remember. Just like Vera Dietz we have 1000s of paper Charlies following us every day. They suffocate us, motivate us, comfort us, every moment of every day. To deal with the loss of Charlie, Vera begins to work more at her pizza delivery job, drink, and <i> live </i> here life to the fullest, dating 23-year-old college drop out. <br /><br />The characters were each unique and the way Vera described them was hilarious. Every character had a quirk that made them seem real. Charlie would write notes and then ceremoniously burn, eat, or pocket them. In the present day chapters you learn that the dead's able to alter reality. Charlie's able to communicate with Vera and change her surroundings so they are filled with paper figures of him or have his writing on a fogged up mirror. Charlie communicates with Vera because she knows something about Charlie's innocence in a crime he supposedly committed moments before his death. The only problem? She hasn't come forward. She wants to help her best friend, but then she remembers how much pain he cause her in the last few months of his life. All he wants for her to do is clear his name. All she wants to do is go back to normal and hold up a sign that says, <i> please ignore Vera Dietz </i>.<br /><br />Throughout the book you realize Vera doesn't have a very good support system. She had lied to herself for 12 years thinking that her parents were happy but once her mother left she knew the truth. All of the things she saw were things she wanted to see. As a young girl she didn't focus on the lost and sad features of her mother throughout the day or how she made her cry without flinching. Now, as an 18-year-old, Vera is left with a shell of a dad who ignores Vera's silent cries for help. <br />She comes home drunk. He <i> doesn't notice </i>. <br />She gets escorted home by a policeman. He doesn't ask her any pressing questions. <br /><br /><blockquote> "If we're supposed to ignore everything that's wrong with our lives, then I can't see how we'll ever make things right.” </blockquote><br /><br />The only problem I had with the book was how A.S. King changed POVs to inanimate objects and spoke to us directly. Vera wouldn't always address the reader directly which I was fine with but once she switched POVs to Vera's dad or Charlie. They would talk directly towards you. Telling you everything they want Vera to know and it just didn't sit well with me. <br /><blockquote> “I want to tell her that the only thing you get from walling yourself in is empty.” </blockquote><br />It pulled me out of the story and sometimes it felt unneeded. The characters would express feelings we should/did pick up from their actions towards Vera. So, it was just a review of what we had already gathered. Then she switched POVs to the Pagoda a famous building in their area. It just didn't flow well with the book. <br /><br />Many of the chapters were set in the past. She would name the chapter "History- (enter age)", this gave the reader a chance to see Charlie and Vera at a young age and only a few moments before his death. It helped you connect with the characters and learn about their living situations. <br /><br />My final thoughts on Please Ignore Vera Dietz is that it is a beautifully written book and deals with grief flawlessly. I will definitely pick up another A.S. King book in the future.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1110417257526945585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_548789391" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/548789391" />
    <a title="Ariel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6536286-ariel"><img alt="Ariel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530557165p2/6536286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/548789391?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ariel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ariel" href="/user/show/6536286-ariel">Ariel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780375865640" href="/book/show/12305758-please-ignore-vera-dietz">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer548789391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4224010204810253980">Well! Another shining read from A.S. King! This has really solidified her as one of my new favourite authors and I definitely look forward to reading more of her books. As you can tell, however, I gave this a 4.4 rating instead of the 5/5 rating I gave Everybody Sees the Ants.. here's why I loved this and didn't!<br/><br/>First off, let's talk about some of the things I loved. Mainly, the writing. A.S. King's way of turning a phrase, the way she shares the things that are going inside of her characters he</span>
  <span id="freeText4224010204810253980" style="display:none">Well! Another shining read from A.S. King! This has really solidified her as one of my new favourite authors and I definitely look forward to reading more of her books. As you can tell, however, I gave this a 4.4 rating instead of the 5/5 rating I gave Everybody Sees the Ants.. here's why I loved this and didn't!<br /><br />First off, let's talk about some of the things I loved. Mainly, the writing. A.S. King's way of turning a phrase, the way she shares the things that are going inside of her characters heads is so raw and gritty and real. It makes me feel like her characters are real people - like her books are memoirs instead of fiction. I love feeling this because it makes me root for the characters, makes me hope that their lives turn out how they want them to turn out. <br /><br />I also love the structure of this book: it's written in tiny chapters, the longest ones being maybe 6 pages, which was cool because I felt like I kept getting new glimpses into the characters minds. They were written from different characters perspectives, although probably 90% are from Vera, but that added a great effect of knowing more than just her thoughts, and also we get some cool perspectives.. including wise inanimate objects and her dead best friend (which I LOVED LOVED).<br /><br />Now, I didn't love this book as much as Everybody Sees the Ants. Why? Because I felt that Vera was not as well developed.. I didn't understand her actions, and most of the time I down-right didn't like her. I loved Lucky, the main character of Everybody Sees the Ants. I wanted to protect him. But with Vera, a lot of the time I wanted to just shove her for not clicking in, for acting so stupidly. Don't misunderstand me - I'm not saying that I need to like a character or like their actions to appreciate them! (Look at the Great Gatsby! I gave that book 5/5 and NONE of the characters there were likable!) My problem is not understanding Vera's decisions. I understood why Daisy gave up on Gatsby even though I hated her for it.. I understood and therefore could appreciate her. But for Vera I didn't understand why she made such foolish decisions, why she didn't take charge, why she hated everyone so much.. and for me, I want to understand the characters so that I can understand their transformations.<br /><br />Overall, I really did like this book a lot. A.S. King has definitely delivered, and I would highly recommend this book to everyone.. especially people who are searching for something along the lines of The Perks of Being a Wallflower or Looking for Alaska.. that raw contemporary feel. Although, admittedly, I'd recommend Everybody Sees the Ants more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4224010204810253980" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Loved the non-linear form of storytelling. Loved the emotional authenticity on every page. The only thing I didn't love was the ending. For me it was intense like, but not quite love. <br/><br/>That's all I can say without revealing (or hinting at) spoilers.</span>

<div id="review_217681133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/217681133" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/217681133?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=death-and-dying">death-and-dying</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer217681133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18014074169820423429"><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/a-s-king/review-please-ignore-vera-dietz.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360389i/711308.jpg' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Once upon a time there was a boy and a girl.<br/>They've been friends since forever, they cared for each other, they played and went to school together, they were inseparable.<br/>They fell in love.<br/>...Until they grew up.<br/>Until things got complicated.<br/>Until there was no longer a boy and a girl.<br/>But only a girl, only Vera..<br/>...Please ignore Vera Dietz.<br/><blockquote>
  <i>"What is the sound of one hand clapping?"<br/>That's how I feel without Charlie. Like one hand clapping</i>
</blockquote><br/>All her life Vera's been thought to 'ignore'.. To ignore</span>
  <span id="freeText18014074169820423429" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/a-s-king/review-please-ignore-vera-dietz.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380360389i/711308.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Once upon a time there was a boy and a girl.<br>They've been friends since forever, they cared for each other, they played and went to school together, they were inseparable.<br>They fell in love.<br>...Until they grew up.<br>Until things got complicated.<br>Until there was no longer a boy and a girl.<br>But only a girl, only Vera..<br>...Please ignore Vera Dietz.<br><blockquote>
  <i>"What is the sound of one hand clapping?"<br>That's how I feel without Charlie. Like one hand clapping</i>
</blockquote><br>All her life Vera's been thought to 'ignore'.. To ignore the kids that were mean, her mother than never cared, her father that was unhappy, the screams from the next door, the bruise on the boy's skin.<br>And all she wanted was to be ignored as well..<br>Until she wasn't anymore.<br><br>What you do when you know someone else's secret?<br>What do you do when the secret is not yours to tell?<br>What do you do when it's just too late?<br><blockquote>
  <i>I'm sorry, but I don't get it. If we're supposed to ignore everything that's wrong with our lives, then I can't see how we'll make things right</i>
</blockquote><br>"Please Ignore Vera Dietz" is a story that deals with some complex subjects. Also it gives us some good lessons about being human, about making mistakes, about trying to change what's wrong, about <em>what-if</em> 's, about being too late, about deciding to do something while you still can...  Because  we can learn from their errors, we could be so much better, we could do so much more.<br><br>I still wonder if the ending would have been different if Vera did something. Anything.. Would it have made any difference at all?<br><br>And this question consumes her as well.<br>Until there's no mystery, until there are no more secrets, until there is nothing left to do.<br><blockquote>
  <i>Two gulps of vodka later, my eyes are watering and my throat automatically grumbles "Ahhhhh" to get rid of the burning. Don't judge me. I'm not getting drunk. I'm coping</i>
</blockquote><br>There are many things I liked about this story. I took the book in my hand and couldn't put it down. I wanted to know more, to understand the characters better, to see what made them do the mistakes they did, to understand why there was no return point for them..<br><br>I wanted more Charlie into the story, I wanted to understand Vera's mother, to know more about Vera's father, to punch Charlie's parents and his new 'friends'. I liked some of the relationships between the characters, but others seemed off. Still, they were all so human with all their mistakes and hopes, they all needed more.<br>It was sad to see Vera and Charlie get more and more distant. I wanted to shake them both and make them see the obvious.<br><br>What I didn't like was the revelation.. Sorry, I just wasn't emotionally invested, not enough. The story seemed too light for what had been promised. The ending should have felt tragic, dramatic.. but for me it was not. I enjoyed the ride, but the destination left me with a bitter-sweet taste in my mouth.. more bitter than sweet.<br><br>As for Jenna, she is still a mystery to me. I didn't get the answers I needed.<br>And I couldn't really understand Charlie. He tried too much to be a better person and then he just gave up.<br>I wish.. I wish they wouldn't have ignored Charlie Kahn.. and so does Vera.<br><br>Rating: 3.5 stars<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" width="361" height="116" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/a-s-king/review-please-ignore-vera-dietz.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="18014074169820423429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
